7/28/24, 4:43 PM - Saif Wiyarوياړ IT Trainer: import pandas as pd
import numpy as np

# Provided data
data = {
    'Date': ['2023-01-01', '2023-01-15', '2023-02-01', '2023-02-20', '2023-03-01', None, '2023-04-01', '2023-04-20', None],
    'Product': ['Laptop', 'Mouse', 'Laptop', 'Keyboard', 'Laptop', None, 'Laptop', None, 'Mouse'],
    'Revenue': [1200, 30, 1500, 70, 1100, None, 1000, None, None],
    'Quantity Sold': [10, 5, 15, 7, 12, None, None, 20, None]
}

# Creating DataFrame
df = pd.DataFrame(data)

# 1. Drop rows if all the columns of a row have missing values
df.dropna(how='all', inplace=True)

# 2. Drop rows if the Product column of a row has missing values
df.dropna(subset=['Product'], inplace=True)

# 3. Fill in the missing values of Revenue and Quantity Sold columns with the arithmetic mean of the respective columns
df['Revenue'].fillna(df['Revenue'].mean(), inplace=True)
df['Quantity Sold'].fillna(df['Quantity Sold'].mean(), inplace=True)

# 4. Filter the data to include only sales for a specific product (e.g., 'Laptop')
laptop_sales = df[df['Product'] == 'Laptop']

# 5. Calculate the total revenue and total quantity sold for the selected product
total_revenue = laptop_sales['Revenue'].sum()
total_quantity_sold = laptop_sales['Quantity Sold'].sum()

# Display the results
print("Filtered DataFrame for 'Laptop':")
print(laptop_sales)
print("\nTotal Revenue for 'Laptop':", total_revenue)
print("Total Quantity Sold for 'Laptop':", total_quantity_sold)
7/28/24, 4:43 PM - Saif Wiyarوياړ IT Trainer: Question one#01 answer
7/28/24, 4:43 PM - Saif Wiyarوياړ IT Trainer: import pandas as pd

# Provided data
data = {
    'CustomerID': [1, 2, 1, 3, 2, 1, 3],
    'PurchaseDate': ['2023-01-05', '2023-01-12', '2023-01-25', '2023-02-03', '2023-02-15', '2023-03-01', '2023-03-20'],
    'Item': ['Laptop', 'Mouse', 'Keyboard', 'Monitor', 'Mouse', 'Laptop', 'Monitor'],
    'Amount': [1200, 30, 70, 150, 30, 1100, 440]
}

# Creating DataFrame
df = pd.DataFrame(data)

# 1. Group the data by CustomerID and calculate the total amount spent per customer
total_amount_per_customer = df.groupby('CustomerID')['Amount'].sum().reset_index()

# 2. Group by Item and calculate the total sales and average sales per product
sales_per_item = df.groupby('Item').agg(Total_Sales=('Amount', 'sum'), Average_Sales=('Amount', 'mean')).reset_index()

# 3. Identify customers who have spent more than $500 in total
customers_spent_more_than_500 = total_amount_per_customer[total_amount_per_customer['Amount'] > 500]

# 4. Normalize the data in the Amount column (Use min-max normalization) and add the new column as "Normalized Amount"
df['Normalized Amount'] = (df['Amount'] - df['Amount'].min()) / (df['Amount'].max() - df['Amount'].min())

# Display the results
print("Total Amount Spent per Customer:")
print(total_amount_per_customer)

print("\nTotal Sales and Average Sales per Product:")
print(sales_per_item)

print("\nCustomers who have Spent More than $500 in Total:")
print(customers_spent_more_than_500)

print("\nDataFrame with Normalized Amount:")
print(df)
7/28/24, 4:43 PM - Saif Wiyarوياړ IT Trainer: Question#02 answer
7/28/24, 4:45 PM - Saif Wiyarوياړ IT Trainer: import numpy as np

# 1. Generate two 2D NumPy arrays (matrices) with shapes (4, 5) and (5, 4) containing random numbers between 5 and 10
matrix1 = np.random.randint(5, 11, size=(4, 5))
matrix2 = np.random.randint(5, 11, size=(5, 4))

# 2. Add the two matrices and multiply the result by a scalar of 15
# First, we need to transpose matrix2 to make it compatible for addition with matrix1
matrix2_transposed = matrix2.T
result_matrix = (matrix1 + matrix2_transposed) * 15

# 3. Compute the standard deviation of the resulting matrix along the rows
std_deviation_rows = np.std(result_matrix, axis=1)

# 4. Compute the sum of the resulting matrix along the columns
sum_columns = np.sum(result_matrix, axis=0)

# 5. Reshape the resulting matrix to get a column vector
column_vector = result_matrix.reshape(-1, 1)

# 6. Reshape the resulting matrix to get a 1D array
one_d_array = result_matrix.reshape(-1)

# Display the results
print("Matrix 1:")
print(matrix1)

print("\nMatrix 2:")
print(matrix2)

print("\nResulting Matrix after Addition and Multiplication by 15:")
print(result_matrix)

print("\nStandard Deviation along the Rows:")
print(std_deviation_rows)

print("\nSum along the Columns:")
print(sum_columns)

print("\nColumn Vector:")
print(column_vector)

print("\n1D Array:")
print(one_d_array)

    {'Name': 'Alice', 'Marks': 85},

    {'Name': 'Charlie', 'Marks': 95},
    {'Name': 'David', 'Marks': 75},

# 1. Filter students who passed the exam scored above 75
passed_students = [student for student in students if student['Marks'] > 75]

# 2. Create a list of tuples containing the student's name and marks for those who passed
passed_students_tuples = [(student['Name'], student['Marks']) for student in passed_students]

# 3. Calculate the grades and create a list of tuples containing the student’s name, marks, and grade
students_with_grades = [
    (student['Name'], student['Marks'], 'P' if student['Marks'] > 75 else 'F') for student in students
]

# Display the results
print("Students who passed (scored above 75):")
print(passed_students)

print("\nList of tuples (Name, Marks) for passed students:")
print(passed_students_tuples)

print("\nList of tuples (Name, Marks, Grade) for all students:")
print(students_with_grades)

9/21/24, 5:24 PM - Saif Wiyarوياړ IT Trainer: Respected Students,

I hope this message finds you well. This is a long message, but a very critical message for all of you.

I have received messages regarding low marks in research or skipping research and opting to enroll in two additional courses instead. If your future plan is to go and study abroad, "Gade C" in research thesis is better than A+ in two additional courses. Don't  miss your research thesis. Don't get afraid of thesis. Skipping thesis can harm your future goal of pursuing research degree from abroad. Remember, with optional courses, your chances of Admission in foreign universities, particularly degrees by research, MS or PhD, decreases by 95%. Whether your research thesis score is low or high, or your research skills are good or weak; in both cases I strongly recommend to complete short online courses from recognized platforms like Coursera, Udemy, MOOCS, Khan Academy, Alison etc.

Here are few of them. You can add further according to your course and background of study. Some of them are free and some are paid. For paid, you can directly write an email to the one who are offering the courses and request for "fee waiver ". They can possibly waive partial or entire fee. All good or bad students should complete these courses and add them to their CVs.

Many students with very high CGPAs (3.5 to 4.0) struggle to secure admission and scholarships due to a lack of research thesis experience or research skills.
 
Here are some additional tips to consider:

Start early: Begin building your research profile as early as possible. You can publish your work in paid research journals or team up with other researchers, the journal will charge APC (Article Publication Charges) for accepting your Abstract/Paper. But be careful of sharing your research work with scammers or predatory journals. The journal must be recognized by HEC Pakistan. You can check out the listing of HEC recognized journals on HJRS website (Google HJRS HEC Pakistan).

Seek guidance: Consult with your professors or academic advisors for guidance and recommendations.

Network: Attend conferences and workshops to connect with researchers in your field. You can develop research ideas and present posters (Search samples of research posters on Google).

Volunteer/Internship (Paid or Unpaid): Consider volunteering for research projects to gain practical experience (CPPR, HRDC etc.)

By following these tips and investing in your research skills, you can significantly increase your chances of securing admission in foreign university and achieving your academic goals by covering the research gap in your profile.

Good luck! Thanks
